<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_fleet">Future fleet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Overground&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Future fleet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2012, TfL announced its intention to procure a fleet of new, longer DMUs, as the Class 172s were unable to handle the passenger demand, causing overcrowding throughout the day. TfL issued a tender for manufacturers to supply eight three- or four-car trains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> However, this proposal was subsequently shelved when the Government announced that the Gospel Oak to Barking line would be electrified, with proposals instead to purchase a fleet of new EMUs.</p>
<p>TfL invited expressions of interest for a total of 39 four-car EMUs in April 2014, with 30 required for the Cheshunt and Chingford routes, 8 for the Gospel Oak to Barking, and 1 for the Romford to Upminster.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chingford_trains_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-chingford_trains-64">[64]</a></sup> Since then the planned procurement has been increased to 45 four-car EMUs, with the additional 6 units intended for the Watford DC Line. The intention is that the five-car Class 378 trains used on the Watford route will be cascaded back to the North London and East London Lines to allow for strengthened services. In June 2015, TfL announced that Bombardier had been awarded the contract to build the new trains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>To increase capacity, Class 378 trains are being lengthened from four coaches to five (the first lengthened train entered service on the East London Line in November 2014, and started to be introduced on the North London Line in April 2015). Some station platforms will need to be lengthened to accommodate the longer trains. TfL's Business Plan provides for the introduction of five-car services on the East London line first, followed on the rest of the electrified Overground network by the end of 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2015 TfL announced that it had placed a £260m order for 45 4-car Bombardier <a href="/wiki/Aventra" title="Aventra">Aventra</a> EMUs, with an option for 24 more, (to be known as <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_710" title="British Rail Class 710">Class 710</a>) similar to those that will be used by <a href="/wiki/Crossrail" title="Crossrail">Crossrail</a>, for use on the West Anglia Routes and the Watford DC, GOBLIN and Romford to Upminster lines, from 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Livery">Livery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Overground&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Livery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Watford_Junction_railway_station_MMB_27_378210.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2624" data-file-width="3936" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Watford_Junction_railway_station_MMB_27_378210.jpg/220px-Watford_Junction_railway_station_MMB_27_378210.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Watford_Junction_railway_station_MMB_27_378210.jpg/330px-Watford_Junction_railway_station_MMB_27_378210.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Watford_Junction_railway_station_MMB_27_378210.jpg/440px-Watford_Junction_railway_station_MMB_27_378210.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Watford_Junction_railway_station_MMB_27_378210.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Wallace Sewell <a href="/wiki/Moquette" title="Moquette">moquette</a> upholstery</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>All Electrostar and Turbostar stock in service now carries Overground livery. It is similar to <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">Underground</a> livery, and consists of white coaches, a longitudinal thick blue stripe and a thin orange stripe along the bottom, London Overground roundels at midpoints along the coaches, black window-surrounds and orange doors. The ends of each unit are painted yellow to comply with National Rail standards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-design-livery_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-design-livery-68">[68]</a></sup> The seat upholstery features a <a href="/wiki/Moquette" title="Moquette">moquette</a> by fabric designers Wallace Sewell.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-transport-museum-moquette-range_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-transport-museum-moquette-range-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>As railway lines have been transferred to London Overground operation, services are sometimes operated using rolling stock inherited from the previous train operating company, and for a temporary period these trains have been branded with transitional livery until they are replaced with newer rolling stock. When the first London Overground services began, they were operated using Silverlink rolling stock which retained Silverlink's purple and lime green livery with yellow doors. The Silverlink logos were removed and Overground banners were added. This rolling stock was eventually completely replaced with new, Overground-branded trains.</p>
<p>Similarly, since the takeover of the Lea Valley Lines, Overground services are being run with trains inherited from Abellio Greater Anglia which are mostly in a plain white livery with red doors. Rather than replace this rolling stock, the trains are to be repainted with full Overground livery and the interiors refurbished with Wallace Sewell upholstery and TfL standard signage and route maps.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Planned_developments">Planned developments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Overground&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Planned developments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:London_Underground_Overground_DLR_Crossrail_map.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1320" data-file-width="2500" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/London_Underground_Overground_DLR_Crossrail_map.svg/220px-London_Underground_Overground_DLR_Crossrail_map.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/London_Underground_Overground_DLR_Crossrail_map.svg/330px-London_Underground_Overground_DLR_Crossrail_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/London_Underground_Overground_DLR_Crossrail_map.svg/440px-London_Underground_Overground_DLR_Crossrail_map.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:London_Underground_Overground_DLR_Crossrail_map.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Tube map showing the planned extension to Barking Riverside and acquisition of the Greenford Branch Line, along with the future addition of <a href="/wiki/Crossrail" title="Crossrail">Crossrail</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="24-hour_services">24-hour services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Overground&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: 24-hour services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>London Overground will run 24-hour trains on Friday and Saturday nights between Highbury &amp; Islington and New Cross Gate from 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LO_24hr_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-LO_24hr-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gospel_Oak_to_Barking_Line">Gospel Oak to Barking Line</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Overground&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Gospel Oak to Barking Line">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Electrification">Electrification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Overground&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Electrification">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>It was announced in June 2013 that £115 million of funding for electrification was being made available as part of upgrades to rail infrastructure included in the government's 2013 spending round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> At the same time Transport for London announced that they had obtained a £90 million commitment from the <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_the_Exchequer" title="Chancellor of the Exchequer">Chancellor of the Exchequer</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Transport" title="Secretary of State for Transport">Secretary of State for Transport</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2015, Network Rail awarded the £56.9m contract to electrify the line to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/J._Murphy_%26_Sons" title="J. Murphy &amp; Sons">J. Murphy &amp; Sons</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> There will be part closures (on weekends and from South Tottenham to Barking) from June to late September 2016, followed by a full closure from October to February 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> There will be further evening and weekend works until late June 2017, and finally around four months of further work to add the wires so that electric <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_710" title="British Rail Class 710">Class 710</a> trains can run from early 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> The line will be electrified using the NR Series 2 OLE range.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Extension_to_Barking_Riverside">Extension to Barking Riverside</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Overground&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Extension to Barking Riverside">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>It was announced as part of the <a href="/wiki/2014_United_Kingdom_budget" title="2014 United Kingdom budget">2014 United Kingdom budget</a> that the Gospel Oak to Barking Line of London Overground would be extended to Barking Riverside.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> £263 million will be spent to extend the line to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brownfield" title="Brownfield">brownfield</a> 10,800-home <a href="/wiki/Barking_Riverside" title="Barking Riverside">Barking Riverside</a> housing development, which <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barking_and_Dagenham_Council" title="Barking and Dagenham Council">Barking and Dagenham Council</a> does not believe to be viable without improved transport connections. The developers of the site, Barking Riverside Limited, will provide £172m towards the project with the remainder coming from <a href="/wiki/Transport_for_London" title="Transport for London">Transport for London</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-railjournal17032016_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-railjournal17032016-79">[79]</a></sup> Construction will start in 2017 and be completed by 2021.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-railjournal17032016_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-railjournal17032016-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Proposed_developments">Proposed developments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Overground&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Proposed developments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Watford_DC_Line_move_to_Bakerloo">Watford DC Line move to Bakerloo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Overground&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Watford DC Line move to Bakerloo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Overground_second.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1126" data-file-width="1247" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Overground_second.png/200px-Overground_second.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Overground_second.png/300px-Overground_second.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Overground_second.png/400px-Overground_second.png 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Overground_second.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
How the London Overground network would look if the Watford DC line transferred to the Bakerloo line and the Primrose Hill link were reinstated.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2007 TfL proposed re-extending the Bakerloo line to <a href="/wiki/Watford_Junction_railway_station" title="Watford Junction railway station">Watford Junction</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> It was suggested that most or all of the line from <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Park_(London)_station" title="Queen's Park (London) station">Queen's Park</a> to Watford Junction would be used exclusively by the <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">London Underground</a>, and London Overground services would be withdrawn.</p>
<p>As part of this change, Overground services would have been diverted at Primrose Hill Junction via <a href="/wiki/Primrose_Hill_railway_station" title="Primrose Hill railway station">Primrose Hill</a> (closed to passengers since 1992) to <a href="/wiki/Camden_Road_railway_station" title="Camden Road railway station">Camden Road</a>, providing a new service between Queen's Park and Stratford.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Had this change taken place, <a href="/wiki/Kilburn_High_Road_railway_station" title="Kilburn High Road railway station">Kilburn High Road</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Hampstead_railway_station" title="South Hampstead railway station">South Hampstead</a> would no longer have had direct services to Euston station, hindering access to central London.</p>
<p>The official Croxley Rail document states, "Bakerloo Line extension to Watford Unlikely" and "TfL’s plans to extend the Bakerloo Line to Watford Junction are on hold indefinitely due to funding and business case constraints". <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Croxley_Link">Croxley Link</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Overground&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Croxley Link">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Funding has since been confirmed for the <a href="/wiki/Croxley_Rail_Link" title="Croxley Rail Link">Croxley Rail Link</a>, diverting the Watford branch of the Metropolitan line to Watford Junction via <a href="/wiki/Watford_High_Street_railway_station" title="Watford High Street railway station">Watford High Street</a>, where it will share tracks with the Overground.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Old_Oak_Common_interchange">Old Oak Common interchange</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Overground&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Old Oak Common interchange">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Crossrail_interchange.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="632" data-file-width="910" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Crossrail_interchange.png/200px-Crossrail_interchange.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Crossrail_interchange.png/300px-Crossrail_interchange.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Crossrail_interchange.png/400px-Crossrail_interchange.png 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Crossrail_interchange.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of the proposed Old Oak Common station</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A long-term plan exists to create an interchange with <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_2" title="High Speed 2">High Speed 2</a> at the proposed <a href="/wiki/Old_Oak_Common_railway_station" title="Old Oak Common railway station">Old Oak Common station</a>. Planning documents issued by the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Transport" title="Department for Transport">Department for Transport</a> suggest that the new station, on a site just south of <a href="/wiki/Willesden_Junction_station" title="Willesden Junction station">Willesden Junction</a>, could open by 2025 and offer connections with the Overground on both the <a href="/wiki/North_London_Line" title="North London Line">North London</a> and West London Lines.</p>
<p>The station would also be served by <a href="/wiki/Crossrail" title="Crossrail">Crossrail</a>, <a href="/wiki/Great_Western_Main_Line" title="Great Western Main Line">Great Western Main Line</a> services and <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Express" title="Heathrow Express">Heathrow Express</a>, and the proposals indicate the possibility of interchange with the <a href="/wiki/Bakerloo_line" title="Bakerloo line">Bakerloo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_line_(London_Underground)" title="Central line (London Underground)">Central lines</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> The plans are supported by the <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Hammersmith_and_Fulham" title="London Borough of Hammersmith and Fulham">London Borough of Hammersmith and Fulham</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<p>In June 2013, the Mayor of London and the London Boroughs of Brent, Ealing and Hammersmith &amp; Fulham released 'vision' consultation documents<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> about the <a href="/wiki/Old_Oak_Common" title="Old Oak Common">Old Oak Common</a> area.</p>
<p>The vision mentions various connections to the London Overground system, linking Old Oak to the North London Line, West London Line, and to two new London Overground branches, to Hounslow, and – via the <a href="/wiki/Dudding_Hill_Line" title="Dudding Hill Line">Dudding Hill Line</a> – to <a href="/wiki/Thameslink" title="Thameslink">Thameslink</a> stations on the <a href="/wiki/Midland_Main_Line" title="Midland Main Line">Midland Main Line</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Thamesmead_extension">Thamesmead extension</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Overground&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Thamesmead extension">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In addition to the plan to extend the Gospel Oak to Barking Line to Barking Riverside, there are also proposals to extend it further under the river to a station in Thamesmead, and then on Abbey Wood to connect with the future Crossrail line.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_acquisitions">Future acquisitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Overground&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Future acquisitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following the completion of the first phase of the London Overground network in December 2012, TfL has expressed its intention to take over the operation of other suburban lines in the London area. As with the original London Overground system, this would involve devolving National Rail services from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rail_franchising_in_Great_Britain" title="Rail franchising in Great Britain">the DfT's franchising system</a> to a TfL-managed concession.</p>
<p>On 21 January 2016 it was announced consideration was being given to the possibility of gradually transferring the suburban services operated by <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_(train_operating_company)" title="Southeastern (train operating company)">Southeastern</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_West_Trains" title="South West Trains">South West Trains</a> and <a href="/wiki/Govia_Thameslink_Railway" title="Govia Thameslink Railway">Govia Thameslink Railway</a> (Great Northern, Thameslink and Southern) to TfL to create a London Suburban Metro.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Past_attempts_on_acquiring_routes">Past attempts on acquiring routes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Overground&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Past attempts on acquiring routes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 2012–13 TfL and the Greater London Authority publicised a proposal for further expansion, identifying a number of services in North-East and South-East London as suitable candidates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mayor-vision_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-mayor-vision-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tfl-expanding_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-tfl-expanding-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cityam231213_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-cityam231213-91">[91]</a></sup> Part of this proposal was fulfilled in May 2015 with the transfer of the Lea Valley and Romford-Upminster Lines out of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liverpool_Street_railway_station" title="Liverpool Street railway station">Liverpool Street</a> to the London Overground network, but TfL's aim of acquiring <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_(train_operating_company)" title="Southeastern (train operating company)">Southeastern</a> metro services currently remains at the proposal stage. Under this scheme, TfL would take over rail services out of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/London_Victoria_railway_station" title="London Victoria railway station">London Victoria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charing_Cross_railway_station" title="Charing Cross railway station">Charing Cross</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cannon_Street_railway_station" title="Cannon Street railway station">Cannon Street</a> to <a href="/wiki/Dartford_railway_station" title="Dartford railway station">Dartford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sevenoaks_railway_station" title="Sevenoaks railway station">Sevenoaks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orpington_railway_station" title="Orpington railway station">Orpington</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hayes_railway_station" title="Hayes railway station">Hayes</a>, but this was rejected following spending cuts imposed by the <a href="/wiki/2013_United_Kingdom_budget" title="2013 United Kingdom budget">2013 United Kingdom budget</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> The possibility of TfL acquiring routes out of <a href="/wiki/London_Bridge_station" title="London Bridge station">London Bridge</a> has also been discussed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cityam231213_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-cityam231213-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2015 the prospect of London Overground expansion was raised again when the <a href="/wiki/London_Assembly" title="London Assembly">London Assembly</a> Transport Committee published a report which advocated the devolution of a number of commuter rail services and the creation of a "South London Metro". In particular, the report identified four rail franchises due for renewal which could be taken over by TfL:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-devolve-report_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-devolve-report-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/South_Western_franchise" title="South Western franchise">South Western franchise</a> from <a href="/wiki/London_Waterloo_station" title="London Waterloo station">London Waterloo</a> to South West London suburbs</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Thameslink,_Southern_and_Great_Northern" title="Thameslink, Southern and Great Northern">Thameslink, Southern and Great Northern</a> franchise (<a href="/wiki/Thameslink_and_Great_Northern" title="Thameslink and Great Northern">Great Northern</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_(train_operating_company)" title="Southern (train operating company)">Southern</a> metro services) out of <a href="/wiki/Moorgate_station" title="Moorgate station">Moorgate</a> to North London and out of London Bridge/Victoria to South London suburbs</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Integrated_Kent" title="Integrated Kent">Integrated Kent</a> franchise (<a href="/wiki/Southeastern_(train_operating_company)" title="Southeastern (train operating company)">Southeastern</a> metro services) out of Victoria/Charing Cross/Cannon Street/London Bridge to South East London suburbs</li>
</ul>
<p><a href="/wiki/Kent_County_Council" title="Kent County Council">Kent County Council</a> had initially expressed opposition to the Dartford route plans on account of limited capacity for Kent express trains being lost to expanded TfL services,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kent-opposed_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-kent-opposed-95">[95]</a></sup> but after negotiations with the London Assembly, reached an agreement to support the proposals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Greenford_Branch">Greenford Branch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Overground&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Greenford Branch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Department for Transport have proposed that Transport for London should take over the <a href="/wiki/Greenford_Branch_Line" title="Greenford Branch Line">Greenford to West Ealing Line</a> in West London. This would bring <a href="/wiki/Greenford_station" title="Greenford station">Greenford</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Greenford_railway_station" title="South Greenford railway station">South Greenford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Castle_Bar_Park_railway_station" title="Castle Bar Park railway station">Castle Bar Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drayton_Green_railway_station" title="Drayton Green railway station">Drayton Green</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Ealing_railway_station" title="West Ealing railway station">West Ealing</a> into the Overground network. Trains on this branch would no longer run directly to Paddington, but would terminate at West Ealing in order to free up line capacity for the forthcoming Crossrail services, and West Ealing station would be reconstructed to allow Greenford branch trains to terminate there. If this proposal were to go ahead, it would happen when the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Western_franchise" title="Greater Western franchise">Greater Western franchise</a> ends in 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=London_Overground&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
